to attach the host endpoint\\n175: // programs to different interfaces.\\n176: func hostRewrites(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, ifName string) (map[string]uint64, map[string]string, error) {\\n177: \\topts := ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep)\\n178: \\tstrings := ELFMapSubstitutions(ep)\\n179: \\n180: \\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ifName)\\n181: \\tif err \\treturn opts, strings, nil\\n224: }\\n225: \\n226: func isObsoleteDev(dev string, devices []string) bool {\\n227: \\t// exclude devices we never attach to/from_netdev to.\\n228: \\tfor _, prefix := ok {\n281: \t\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(bpfFilter.Name, symbolFromHostNetdevEp) {\n282: \t\t\t\t\tingressDevs = append(ingressDevs, l)\n283: \t\t\t\t}\n284: \t\t\t}\n285: \t\t}\n286: \n287: \t\tegressFilters, err := safenetlink.FilterList(l, directionToParent(dirEgress))\n288: \t\tif err != nil {\n289: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"listing egress filters: %w\", err)\n290: \t\t}\n291: \t\tfor _, filter := range egressFilters {\n292: \t\t\tif bpfFilter, ok := filter.(*netlink.BpfFilter); Attaches cil_from_netdev to ingress and\n420: // optionally cil_to_netdev to egress if enabled features require it.\n421: func attachNetworkDevices(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n422: \tdevices := cfg.DeviceNames()\n423: \n424: \t// Selectively attach bpf_host to cilium_wg0.\n425: \tif option.Config.NeedBPFHostOnWireGuardDevice() {\n426: \t\tdevices = append(devices, wgTypes.IfaceName)\n427: \t}\n428: \n429: \t// Replace programs on physical devices, ignoring devices that don't exist.\n430: \tfor _, device := range devices {\n431: \t\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(device)\n432: \t\tif err != nil {\n433: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).WithField(\"device\", device).Warn(\"Link does not exist\")\n434: \t\t\tcontinue\n435: \t\t}\n436: \n437: \t\tlinkDir := bpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), iface)\n438: \n439: \t\tconsts, renames, err := hostRewrites(cfg, ep, device)\n440: \t\tif err != nil {\n441: \t\t\treturn err\n442: \t\t}\n443: \n444: \t\tvar netdevObj hostNetdevObjects\n445: \t\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&netdevObj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n446: \t\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n447: \t\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n448: \t\t\t},\n449: \t\t\tMapRenames: renames,\n450: \t\t\tConstants:  consts,\n451: \t\t})\n452: \t\tif err != nil {\n453: \t\t\treturn err\n454: \t\t}\n455: \t\tdefer netdevObj.Close()\n456: \n457: \t\t// Attach cil_from_netdev to ingress.\n458: \t\tif err := attachSKBProgram(iface, netdevObj.FromNetdev, symbolFromHostNetdevEp,\n459: \t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n482: \t\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", device, err)\n483: \t\t\t\t}\n484: \t\t\t}\n485: \t\t} else {\n486: \t\t\t// Remove any previously attached device from egress path if BPF\n487: \t\t\t// NodePort and host firewall are disabled.\n488: \t\t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(iface, symbolToHostNetdevEp, linkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n489: \t\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n490: \t\t\t}\n491: \t\t}\n492: \n493: \t\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n494: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n495: \t\t}\n496: \t}\n497: \n498: \t// Call immediately after attaching programs to make it obvious that a\n499: \t// program was wrongfully detached due to a bug or misconfiguration.\n500: \tif err := removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms(devices); err != nil {\n501: \t\tlog.WithError(err).Error(\"Failed to remove obsolete netdev programs\")\n502: \t}\n503: \n504: \treturn nil\n505: }\n506: \n507: // reloadEndpoint loads programs in spec into the device used by ep.\n508: //\n509: // spec is modified by the method and it is the callers responsibility to copy\n510: // it if necessary.\n511: func reloadEndpoint(ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n512: \tdevice := ep.InterfaceName()\n513: \n514: \tvar obj lxcObjects\n515: \tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&obj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n516: \t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n517: \t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n518: \t\t},\n519: \t\tMapRenames: ELFMapSubstitutions(ep),\n520: \t\tConstants:  ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep),\n521: \t})\n522: \tif err != nil {\n523: \t\treturn err\n524: \t}\n525: \tdefer obj.Close()\n526: \n527: \t// Insert policy programs before attaching entrypoints to tc hooks.\n528: \t// Inserting a policy program is considered an attachment, since it makes\n529: \t// the code reachable by bpf_host when it evaluates policy for the endpoint.\n530: \t// All internal tail call plumbing needs to be done before this point.\n531: \t// If the agent dies uncleanly after the first program has been inserted,\n532: \t// the endpoint's connectivity will be partially broken or exhibit undefined\n533: \t// behaviour like missed tail calls or drops.\n534: \tif err := obj.PolicyMap.Update(uint32(ep.GetID()), obj.PolicyProg, ebpf.UpdateAny); err != nil {\n555: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"interface %s egress: %w\", device, err)\n556: \t\t}\n557: \t} else {\n558: \t\tif err := detachSKBProgram(iface, symbolToEndpoint, linkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n559: \t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n560: \t\t}\n561: \t}\n562: \n563: \tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n564: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n565: \t}\n566: \n567: \tif ep.RequireEndpointRoute() {\n568: \t\tscopedLog := ep.Logger(subsystem).WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n569: \t\t\tlogfields.Interface: device,\n570: \t\t})\n571: \t\tif ip := ep.IPv4Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n572: \t\t\tif err := upsertEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip)); err != nil {\n573: \t\t\t\tscopedLog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Failed to upsert route\")\n574: \t\t\t}\n575: \t\t}\n576: \t\tif ip := ep.IPv6Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n577: \t\t\tif err := upsertEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip)); err != nil {\n578: \t\t\t\tscopedLog.WithError(err).Warn(\"Failed to upsert route\")\n579: \t\t\t}\n580: \t\t}\n581: \t}\n582: \n583: \treturn nil\n584: }\n585: \n586: func replaceOverlayDatapath(ctx context.Context, cArgs []string, device netlink.Link) error {\n587: \tif err := compileOverlay(ctx, cArgs); err != nil {\n682: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n683: \t}\n684: \treturn nil\n685: }\n686: \n687: // ReloadDatapath reloads the BPF datapath programs for the specified endpoint.\n688: //\n689: // It attempts to find a pre-compiled\n690: // template datapath object to use, to avoid a costly compile operation.\n691: // Only if there is no existing template that has the same configuration\n692: // parameters as the specified endpoint, this function will compile a new\n693: // template for this configuration.\n694: //\n695: // This function will block if the cache does not contain an entry for the\n696: // same EndpointConfiguration and multiple goroutines attempt to concurrently\n697: // CompileOrLoad with the same configuration parameters. When the first\n698: // goroutine completes compilation of the template, all other CompileOrLoad\n699: // invocations will be released.\n700: func (l *loader) ReloadDatapath(ctx context.Context, ep datapath.Endpoint, cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, stats *metrics.SpanStat) (string, error) {\n701: \tdirs := directoryInfo{\n702: \t\tLibrary: option.Config.BpfDir,\n703: \t\tRuntime: option.Config.StateDir,\n704: \t\tState:   ep.StateDir(),\n705: \t\tOutput:  ep.StateDir(),\n706: \t}\n707: \n708: \tspec, hash, err := l.templateCache.fetchOrCompile(ctx, cfg, ep, &dirs, stats)\n709: \tif err != nil {\n710: \t\treturn \"\", err\n711: \t}\n712: \n713: \tif ep.IsHost() {\n714: \t\t// Reload bpf programs on cilium_host and cilium_net.\n715: \t\tstats.BpfLoadProg.Start()\n716: \t\terr = reloadHostEndpoint(cfg, ep, spec)\n717: \t\tstats.BpfLoadProg.End(err == nil)\n718: \n719: \t\tl.hostDpInitializedOnce.Do(func() {\n720: \t\t\tlog.Debug(\"Initialized host datapath\")\n721: \t\t\tclose(l.hostDpInitialized)\n722: \t\t})\n723: \n724: \t\treturn hash, err\n725: \t}\n726: \n727: \t// Reload an lxc endpoint program.\n728: \tstats.BpfLoadProg.Start()\n729: \terr = reloadEndpoint(ep, spec)\n730: \tstats.BpfLoadProg.End(err == nil)\n731: \treturn hash, err\n732: }\n733: \n734: // Unload removes the datapath specific program aspects\n735: func (l *loader) Unload(ep datapath.Endpoint) {\n736: \tif ep.RequireEndpointRoute() {\n737: \t\tif ip := ep.IPv4Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n738: \t\t\tremoveEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip))\n739: \t\t}\n740: \n741: \t\tif ip := ep.IPv6Address(); ip.IsValid() {\n742: \t\t\tremoveEndpointRoute(ep, *netipx.AddrIPNet(ip))\n743: \t\t}\n744: \t}\n745: \n746: \tlog := log.WithField(logfields.EndpointID, ep.StringID())\n747: \n748: \t// Remove legacy tc attachments.\n749: \tlink, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ep.InterfaceName())\n750: \tif err == nil {\n751: \t\tif err := removeTCFilters(link, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS); err != nil {\n752: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"Removing ingress filter from interface %s\", ep.InterfaceName())\n753: \t\t}\n754: \t\tif err := removeTCFilters(link, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_EGRESS); err != nil {\n755: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"Removing egress filter from interface %s\", ep.InterfaceName())\n756: \t\t}\n757: \t}\n758: \n759: \t// If Cilium and the kernel support tcx to attach TC programs to the\n760: \t// endpoint's veth device, its bpf_link object is pinned to a per-endpoint\n761: \t// bpffs directory. as it locks IPCache, which\n635: \t// leads to a deadlock if endpoint lock is held.\n636: \trules := e.owner.GetDNSRules(e.ID)\n637: \n638: \tstats.waitingForLock.Start()\n639: \terr = e.lockAlive()\n640: \tstats.waitingForLock.End(err == nil)\n641: \tif err != nil {\n642: \t\treturn err\n643: \t}\n644: \n645: \tdefer e.unlock()\n646: \n647: \t// In the first ever regeneration of the endpoint, the conntrack table\n648: \t// is cleaned from the new endpoint IPs as it is guaranteed that any\n649: \t// pre-existing connections using that IP are now invalid.\n650: \tif !e.ctCleaned {\n651: \t\tgo func() {\n652: \t\t\tif !e.isProperty(PropertyFakeEndpoint) &&\n653: \t\t\t\toption.Config.DatapathMode != datapathOption.DatapathModeLBOnly {\n654: \t\t\t\tipv4 := ctmap.Exists(e, ipv4, ipv6)\n659: \t\t\t\t}\n660: \t\t\t\tif exists {\n661: \t\t\t\t\te.scrubIPsInConntrackTable()\n662: \t\t\t\t}\n663: \t\t\t}\n664: \t\t\tclose(datapathRegenCtxt.ctCleaned)\n665: \t\t}()\n666: \t} else {\n667: \t\tclose(datapathRegenCtxt.ctCleaned)\n668: \t}\n669: \n670: \t// Set the computed policy as the \"incoming\" policy. This can fail if\n671: \t// the endpoint's security identity changed during or after policy calculation.\n672: \t// Note that the incoming policy can be the same as the previous policy in cases\n673: \t// where an unnecessary policy computation was skipped. In that case\n674: \t// e.desiredPolicy == e.realizedPolicy also after this call.\n675: \tif err := e.setDesiredPolicy(datapathRegenCtxt); err != nil {\n676: \t\treturn err\n677: \t}\n678: \t// Mark the new desired policy as ready when done before the lock is released\n679: \tif e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy {\n680: \t\tdefer e.desiredPolicy.Ready()\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \t// Apply pending policy map changes so that desired map is up-to-date before\n684: \t// syncing the maps below.\n685: \tif e.SecurityIdentity != nil {\n686: \t\t_ = e.updateAndOverrideEndpointOptions(nil)\n687: \n688: \t\t// Apply incremental changes to desiredPolicy and Configure the new network policy\n689: \t\t// with the proxies.\n690: \t\t//\n691: \t\t// If we have a new policy, it is likely that incremental updates were applied to\n692: \t\t// the old policy while we were waiting for the endpoint lock. Note that it\n703: \t\t// is possible for further incremental changes to be applied before and after the\n704: \t\t// bpf policy maps have been synchronized for the new policy.\n705: \t\terr = e.applyPolicyMapChangesLocked(regenContext, e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy)\n706: \t\tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, ErrPolicyEntryMaxExceeded) {\n707: \t\t\treturn err\n708: \t\t}\n709: \n710: \t\t// Signal computation of the initial Envoy policy if not done yet\n711: \t\te.initialPolicyComputedLocked()\n712: \t}\n713: \n714: \tcurrentDir := datapathRegenCtxt.currentDir\n715: \tnextDir := datapathRegenCtxt.nextDir\n716: \n717: \t// We cannot obtain the rules while e.mutex is held, because obtaining\n718: \t// fresh DNSRules requires the IPCache lock (which must not be taken while\n719: \t// holding e.mutex to avoid deadlocks). {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_014gqCoozR5bS4MUkFf1qDez","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01CEe8hYkC8NwGTCSSRwU2Tt","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation\n\n## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n\n### How eBPF programs are compiled, loaded, and attached independently on each node\n\n**Component: Compilation**\n\nEach Cilium agent running on a node independently compiles eBPF programs locally using the `loader` component:\n\n1. **Local Kernel Probing** (`pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:135-157`):\n   - `getBPFCPU()` function probes the kernel at runtime to detect available BPF ISA versions\n   - Detects support for BPF v3, v2, or v1 based on kernel helpers: `probes.HaveV3ISA()`, `probes.HaveV2ISA()`\n   - This allows per-node CPU-specific optimizations based on kernel capabilities\n   - Result is stored in `nameBPFCPU` variable, making compilation node-specific\n\n2. **Template-Based Compilation** (`pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:26-94`):\n   - `objectCache` maintains a per-node cache of compiled eBPF templates\n   - `UpdateDatapathHash()` monitors node configuration changes (kernel version, enabled features)\n   - When configuration changes, the cache is invalidated and recompilation is triggered\n   - Hash is calculated per-node from `LocalNodeConfiguration`\n\n3. **Compilation Process** (`pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:170-257`):\n   - `compile()` function uses clang to compile BPF C code into object files\n   - Node configuration (kernel MHz, number of CPUs) is injected via `-D` compiler flags\n   - Headers are generated from node-specific state in `pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:141-142`\n   - Each compilation produces a node-local object file stored in the state directory\n\n**Component: Loading and Attachment**\n\n4. **Per-Endpoint Loading** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:700-732`):\n   - `ReloadDatapath()` loads compiled BPF programs for a specific endpoint\n   - `templateCache.fetchOrCompile()` retrieves or generates a template for the endpoint configuration\n   - Templates are cached locally at `<StateDir>/templates/` (see `pkg/defaults/defaults.go:56-57`)\n   - Each endpoint gets its own policy programs loaded independently\n\n5. **Program Attachment via TC/XDP** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:507-584`, `loader.go:319-334`):\n   - Programs attached at Linux Traffic Control (tc) ingress/egress hooks\n   - `attachSKBProgram()` attaches to endpoint's veth device interface\n   - `attachCiliumHost()` and `attachNetworkDevices()` attach host/device programs\n   - Each attachment is per-interface, per-direction, per-node\n\n**Key Insight**: Node-specific configuration affects compilation (kernel features, CPU variant) but failures are isolated because each node compiles independently before any cluster-wide policy is applied.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### How Cilium's deployment model ensures per-node isolation\n\n**DaemonSet Deployment** (`install/kubernetes/cilium/templates/cilium-agent/daemonset.yaml`):\n\n1. **One Pod Per Node**:\n   - Cilium is deployed as a Kubernetes DaemonSet (not Deployment)\n   - Each node runs exactly one Cilium agent pod\n   - If the DaemonSet is updated, each pod is updated independently, not rolled out cluster-wide\n   - Failure of one node's pod does NOT prevent other nodes' pods from running\n\n2. **Per-Node BPF Filesystem Mount** (`daemonset.yaml:809-815`, `daemonset.yaml:602-606`):\n   - Each Cilium pod mounts the host's BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf`\n   - This is a per-node filesystem; each node has its own `/sys/fs/bpf` on the host\n   - BPF maps and programs are stored per-node in `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/`\n   - If one node's BPF filesystem is corrupted, other nodes' filesystems are unaffected\n\n3. **Independent Agent Initialization** (`daemon/cmd/daemon_main.go`, `daemon/cmd/daemon.go`):\n   - Each agent initializes independently in `func newDaemon()`\n   - Calls `d.initMaps()` (`daemon/cmd/datapath.go:145-156`) to open/create BPF maps\n   - Maps are created in the node-local BPF filesystem\n   - If map initialization fails on node A, node B's maps are unaffected\n\n4. **Compilation Lock Per Agent** (`daemon/cmd/daemon.go:119-122`, `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:86`):\n   - Each agent maintains a `compilationLock` to serialize eBPF compilation\n   - Compilation happens locally; no cluster-wide coordination\n   - One node's compilation failure doesn't block other nodes' compilation\n\n**Control Plane / Data Plane Split**:\n\n5. **Control Plane**: Kubernetes API Server (central, cluster-wide)\n6. **Data Plane**: eBPF programs on each node (distributed, per-node)\n   - Policy definitions are distributed via Kubernetes API as CRDs\n   - But enforcement happens independently per-node through locally-compiled eBPF\n   - Each node enforces policies using its own compiled eBPF bytecode\n\n**Fallback Behavior** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:280-281`, `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:141-157`):\n- If a node cannot compile eBPF for its kernel version, it logs an error and continues\n- Other nodes continue to operate normally\n- The failing node may degrade to fallback mode or log policy enforcement failures\n- No cascade to other nodes\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How cluster-wide CRDs are translated to per-node eBPF enforcement\n\n**Policy Distribution** (Kubernetes API):\n\n1. **Cluster-Wide Policy Resources**:\n   - `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (namespaced) and `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy` (cluster-wide)\n   - These are standard Kubernetes Custom Resource Definitions (CRDs)\n   - Stored in etcd, accessible to all agents via Kubernetes API watch\n   - Distribution is handled by Kubernetes API server, not Cilium\n\n2. **Per-Node Policy Watcher** (`daemon/cmd/daemon.go`, `pkg/k8s/watchers/watcher.go`):\n   - Each agent runs a watcher on the Kubernetes API\n   - All agents watch the same policy resources\n   - When a policy changes, all agents are notified simultaneously via API watch\n\n**Policy Translation (Per-Node Compilation)**:\n\n3. **Policy to eBPF Translation** (`pkg/policy/`, `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:529-584`):\n   - Each agent independently translates policies into eBPF bytecode\n   - Translation happens in `Endpoint.SyncPolicy()` and `policyMapSync()`\n   - Policy state is stored in `desiredPolicy` and `realizedPolicy` per endpoint\n   - Translation is deterministic but node-local (no cross-node dependencies)\n\n4. **Per-Endpoint Policy Maps** (`pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go:31-39`):\n   - Each endpoint gets a policy map: `cilium_policy_v2_<endpoint-id>`\n   - Maps are created locally on each node\n   - Policy keys: `(identity, traffic_direction, protocol, port, prefix_len)`\n   - Policy values: allow/deny decisions with proxy port info\n   - Maps are stored per-endpoint in node-local BPF filesystem\n\n5. **Endpoint Regeneration** (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go`, `pkg/endpoint/regenerator.go`):\n   - When a policy changes, affected endpoints are regenerated\n   - Regeneration happens per-endpoint, per-node\n   - Each agent calculates affected endpoints independently\n   - Endpoint compilation via `ReloadDatapath()` with endpoint-specific configuration\n   - Template hashing in `pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:170` ensures consistency within a node\n\n**Why One Node Failure Doesn't Propagate**:\n\n6. **Independent Translation**:\n   - Policy resource exists in Kubernetes API (shared)\n   - But translation to eBPF happens independently per-node\n   - If node A's compiler/verifier rejects a program, node B's compiler still succeeds\n   - Node A logs the error but doesn't affect node B's policy enforcement\n\n7. **Endpoint-Specific Configuration** (`pkg/datapath/types/config.go`):\n   - Each node has `LocalNodeConfiguration` with kernel-specific settings\n   - Endpoints use this node-local config during compilation\n   - Same policy + different kernel config = potentially different compiled eBPF\n   - This allows graceful degradation per-node\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### How eBPF map state is isolated across nodes\n\n**Map Creation and Scoping**:\n\n1. **Per-Node BPF Filesystem Hierarchy** (`pkg/datapath/loader/paths.go:15-75`):\n   - Maps are pinned to `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/` on each node (host-level path)\n   - Endpoint maps: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>/`\n   - Device maps: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/devices/<device-name>/`\n   - Links directory: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>/links/`\n   - Each path is node-local (on host filesystem, not in container)\n\n2. **Per-Endpoint Maps** (`pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go:31-39`):\n   - Policy map name: `cilium_policy_v2_<endpoint-id>`\n   - Endpoint ID is assigned per-container per-node (e.g., 1-65535)\n   - Same container on different nodes gets different endpoint IDs\n   - Maps with different IDs don't interact\n\n3. **Global vs. Per-Endpoint Maps**:\n   - **Global maps** (shared across endpoints on a node):\n     - `cilium_call_policy`: Program array for policy tail calls (per-node)\n     - `cilium_ct_<dir>_<version>`: Connection tracking (per-node, shared)\n     - `cilium_ipcache`: IP to identity mapping (per-node, shared via BPF filesystem)\n   - **Per-Endpoint maps**:\n     - `cilium_policy_v2_<epid>`: Policy decisions (per-endpoint, per-node)\n     - `cilium_calls_<epid>`: Custom calls (per-endpoint, per-node)\n\n4. **BPF Filesystem Pinning** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:345-376`, `loader.go:516-520`):\n   - Maps are pinned to the BPF filesystem during load in `bpf.LoadAndAssign()`\n   - Pin path includes node-local state directory: `bpf.TCGlobalsPath()`\n   - When a map is pinned, subsequent accesses refer to the pinned path\n   - **Isolation mechanism**: Different nodes have different host filesystems\n\n**Network Namespace Isolation**:\n\n5. **Container Network Namespace**:\n   - Each container runs in a separate network namespace (on host)\n   - Host-facing veth device is in host namespace\n   - eBPF programs attach to veth device, enforce policy in host namespace\n   - TC hooks on veth enforce ingress/egress policy for the container\n   - **Isolation**: eBPF programs access maps via file descriptor, which references the pinned path on the node\n\n6. **Map State Independence**:\n   - If node A fails to create a map, node B's maps are unaffected\n   - Maps are created independently during agent init (`daemon/cmd/datapath.go:145-156`)\n   - Creation happens in parallel (no cross-node synchronization)\n   - Map entries are not synchronized across nodes (except through policy updates)\n\n**Failure Scenarios**:\n\n7. **Map Full / Overflow**:\n   - If an endpoint's policy map overflows on node A, only that endpoint on node A is affected\n   - Other endpoints on node A can still write to their maps\n   - All endpoints on node B operate normally (their maps are separate)\n   - Agent can lockdown the endpoint if configured (`option.EnableEndpointLockdownOnPolicyOverflow`)\n\n8. **Map Corruption / Loss**:\n   - If node A's BPF filesystem is unmounted, maps are lost on node A\n   - Node B's BPF filesystem (on different host) is unaffected\n   - On node A restart, maps are recreated from scratch (endpoints reinitialized)\n   - No cluster-wide impact\n\n9. **Kernel Verifier Rejection**:\n   - If a program is rejected by kernel verifier on node A (e.g., due to kernel version mismatch)\n   - Node B's kernel may accept the same program (different kernel version, different verifier rules)\n   - eBPF source is compiled node-locally with node-specific parameters\n   - Compilation can succeed on node B even if it fails on node A\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Files and References\n\n#### Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n- **Compilation Logic**: `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:135-257`\n  - `getBPFCPU()` function probes the kernel at runtime to detect available BPF ISA versions\n   - Detects support for BPF v3, v2, or v1 based on kernel helpers: `probes.HaveV3ISA()`, `probes.HaveV2ISA()`\n   - This allows per-node CPU-specific optimizations based on kernel capabilities\n   - Result is stored in `nameBPFCPU` variable, making compilation node-specific\n\n2. **Template-Based Compilation** (`pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:26-94`):\n   - `objectCache` maintains a per-node cache of compiled eBPF templates\n   - `UpdateDatapathHash()` monitors node configuration changes (kernel version, enabled features)\n   - When configuration changes, the cache is invalidated and recompilation is triggered\n   - Hash is calculated per-node from `LocalNodeConfiguration`\n\n3. **Compilation Process** (`pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:170-257`):\n   - `compile()` function uses clang to compile BPF C code into object files\n   - Node configuration (kernel MHz, number of CPUs) is injected via `-D` compiler flags\n   - Headers are generated from node-specific state in `pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:141-142`\n   - Each compilation produces a node-local object file stored in the state directory\n\n**Component: Loading and Attachment**\n\n4. **Per-Endpoint Loading** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:700-732`):\n   - `ReloadDatapath()` loads compiled BPF programs for a specific endpoint\n   - `templateCache.fetchOrCompile()` retrieves or generates a template for the endpoint configuration\n   - Templates are cached locally at `<StateDir>/templates/` (see `pkg/defaults/defaults.go:56-57`)\n   - Each endpoint gets its own policy programs loaded independently\n\n5. **Program Attachment via TC/XDP** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:507-584`, `loader.go:319-334`):\n   - Programs attached at Linux Traffic Control (tc) ingress/egress hooks\n   - `attachSKBProgram()` attaches to endpoint's veth device interface\n   - `attachCiliumHost()` and `attachNetworkDevices()` attach host/device programs\n   - Each attachment is per-interface, per-direction, per-node\n\n**Key Insight**: Node-specific configuration affects compilation (kernel features, CPU variant) but failures are isolated because each node compiles independently before any cluster-wide policy is applied.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### How Cilium's deployment model ensures per-node isolation\n\n**DaemonSet Deployment** (`install/kubernetes/cilium/templates/cilium-agent/daemonset.yaml`):\n\n1. **One Pod Per Node**:\n   - Cilium is deployed as a Kubernetes DaemonSet (not Deployment)\n   - Each node runs exactly one Cilium agent pod\n   - If the DaemonSet is updated, each pod is updated independently, not rolled out cluster-wide\n   - Failure of one node's pod does NOT prevent other nodes' pods from running\n\n2. **Per-Node BPF Filesystem Mount** (`daemonset.yaml:809-815`, `daemonset.yaml:602-606`):\n   - Each Cilium pod mounts the host's BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf`\n   - This is a per-node filesystem; each node has its own `/sys/fs/bpf` on the host\n   - BPF maps and programs are stored per-node in `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/`\n   - If one node's BPF filesystem is corrupted, other nodes' filesystems are unaffected\n\n3. **Independent Agent Initialization** (`daemon/cmd/daemon_main.go`, `daemon/cmd/daemon.go`):\n   - Each agent initializes independently in `func newDaemon()`\n   - Calls `d.initMaps()` (`daemon/cmd/datapath.go:145-156`) to open/create BPF maps\n   - Maps are created in the node-local BPF filesystem\n   - If map initialization fails on node A, node B's maps are unaffected\n\n4. **Compilation Lock Per Agent** (`daemon/cmd/daemon.go:119-122`, `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:86`):\n   - Each agent maintains a `compilationLock` to serialize eBPF compilation\n   - Compilation happens locally; no cluster-wide coordination\n   - One node's compilation failure doesn't block other nodes' compilation\n\n**Control Plane / Data Plane Split**:\n\n5. **Control Plane**: Kubernetes API Server (central, cluster-wide)\n6. **Data Plane**: eBPF programs on each node (distributed, per-node)\n   - Policy definitions are distributed via Kubernetes API as CRDs\n   - But enforcement happens independently per-node through locally-compiled eBPF\n   - Each node enforces policies using its own compiled eBPF bytecode\n\n**Fallback Behavior** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:280-281`, `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:141-157`):\n- If a node cannot compile eBPF for its kernel version, it logs an error and continues\n- Other nodes continue to operate normally\n- The failing node may degrade to fallback mode or log policy enforcement failures\n- No cascade to other nodes\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How cluster-wide CRDs are translated to per-node eBPF enforcement\n\n**Policy Distribution** (Kubernetes API):\n\n1. **Cluster-Wide Policy Resources**:\n   - I've completed a comprehensive investigation of Cilium's eBPF fault isolation architecture and saved the detailed analysis to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.\n\n## Summary\n\nThe investigation explains how Cilium ensures that eBPF program failures on one Kubernetes node don't propagate cluster-wide:\n\n**Key Findings:**\n\n1. **Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle**: Each Cilium agent independently probes its kernel (ISA version detection), compiles eBPF programs locally with node-specific parameters, and loads them. Compilation failures are node-local.\n\n2. **Deployment Architecture**: Cilium runs as a Kubernetes DaemonSet with one pod per node. Each agent has an independent `compilationLock` and initializes maps locally in `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/`. One node's BPF filesystem is isolated from others.\n\n3. **Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement**: While cluster-wide `CiliumNetworkPolicy` resources are distributed via Kubernetes API, **each node independently translates them to eBPF bytecode**. If node A's kernel verifier rejects a program, node B's compilation can still succeed.\n\n4. **eBPF Map Scoping**: Maps are pinned to per-node directories (`/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>/`). Each endpoint on each node gets a unique endpoint ID and separate maps.
